Italy, Austria, and Hungary Reach Understanding

National News Agency, Berlin, 13th: According to a Rome dispatch, negotiations between Italy, Austria, and Hungary on concluding a credit agreement to promote commerce have reached an understanding in principle. German newspapers expressed great welcome to this news, believing it to be a good omen for the Geneva Conference, because in the future, in the debate over the German-Austrian customs union, this can be used to unite Germany, Austria, Hungary, and Italy to counter the alliance of France, Poland, and the Little Entente, and allow Britain to act as a mediator. The German-Austrian tax agreement plan has stipulated from the beginning that other countries can be invited to join, without geographical restrictions. This also proves that France's accusation that Germany and Austria intend to establish a new Central European state is completely fabricated.

We respectfully submit our words and ask for your consideration. Shanxi Army's Military Pay to Be Substantially Resolved 82

Zhang Xueliang Telegraphed Shanxi Agreeing to Allocate Funds

Taiyuan Correspondence: Since returning to Shanxi from Beiping, the Shanxi generals have been waiting for Shang Zhen to return to negotiate issues such as troop reduction and military pay, so they have been staying in Shanxi. Regarding the issue of military pay, Zhang Xueliang recently telegraphed, agreeing to pay from May 1st. The generals are extremely grateful and plan to jointly telegraph Zhang to express their gratitude and request that the funds they are entitled to be allocated as soon as possible to alleviate their urgent needs. As for the weather in the province, there has been widespread rainfall in the past three days, so the people's hearts are gradually stabilizing. This is also a piece of good news in the midst of the precarious situation in Shanxi. (May 9th)

Nearly Thirty Years of Tibetan History 83

Published After the Panchen Lama's Arrival in Beijing

Urging the Government to Resolve Tibetan Affairs

Since the time of Tsongkhapa, who founded the Yellow Sect during the Yongle reign of the Ming Dynasty, the Dalai Lama and the Panchen Lama, as his two disciples, have resided in the front and rear Tibet respectively, managing Tibetan affairs. In the 57th year of the Kangxi reign of the Qing Dynasty, the Dzungars invaded front Tibet, and the Dalai Lama took refuge in the塔尔寺 Ta'er Monastery in Xining. The Qing court ordered 傳爾丹噶爾弼 Chu'er Dan Ga'er Bi and others to lead troops from Qinghai and Sichuan in two routes to attack Tibet. The Dzungar army was defeated, and the Dalai Lama was reinstated in the 59th year of Kangxi. Two thousand Mongolian soldiers were left to garrison Tibet but were soon withdrawn. In the 7th year of the Yongzheng reign, the rebellion of 阿爾布巴 A'er Bu Ba was quelled, and two high officials, a principal and a deputy, were sent with two thousand soldiers from Sichuan and Shaanxi to garrison front and rear Tibet. In the 15th year of the Qianlong reign, the number of troops stationed in Tibet was increased by fifteen hundred. In the 22nd year, 伊犂 Yili was pacified, and front Tibet was free from the troubles of the Dzungars. In the 55th year, the Gurkhas invaded rear Tibet, and the Panchen Lama took refuge in front Tibet. The Qing court ordered 福康安 Fu Kang'an and 海蘭察 Hai Lan Cha to lead troops from Qinghai to rear Tibet, defeating the Gurkhas and entering their territory for one hundred and sixty miles. The Gurkhas surrendered, and the Panchen Lama was reinstated. Three thousand Tibetan soldiers and one thousand Han and Mongolian soldiers were left to garrison Tibet. Regulations were also established for the two high officials, treating them equally with the Dalai Lama and the Panchen Lama, with unified authority. Rear Tibet was thus free from the troubles of the Gurkhas. From then on, China and Tibet were at peace for more than a hundred years. During the 17th year of the Guangxu reign, 德爾智 De'er Zhi, advocating pro-Russian ideas, served as a lecturer to the Dalai Lama, which aroused the ambition of Britain. Consequently, in the 29th year, they started a war in Lhasa. The Dalai Lama was defeated and sought help from Russia, going to Kulun to meet 哲布尊丹巴 Zhe Bu Zun Dan Ba, who introduced him to the Russian representative and telegraphed St. Petersburg. The Russian Tsar then presented four hundred sets of cavalry uniforms and equipment. The Qing court, upon learning of this, revoked the Dalai Lama's title and appointed the Panchen Lama to concurrently manage front Tibet, and secretly ordered the Kulun minister to intercept the Dalai Lama in the 丰熱吐 Feng Re Tu area of Outer Mongolia. The Dalai Lama, on his way, heard that Russia had been defeated by Japan, and then requested an audience and asked for troops to be sent to Tibet for defense. The Qing court advised the Dalai Lama to return to Tibet. The Dalai Lama then took the route through Xining. It was not until the tenth month of the first year of Xuantong that he arrived in Lhasa. Because of a strained relationship with 聯豫 Lian Yu, the resident minister in Tibet, he intended to go back on his word and obstruct the entry of troops into Tibet. However, in the sixth month of that year, Zhao Erxun, the governor of Sichuan, had already received an imperial decree, ordering Zhong Ying to lead a combined brigade to enter Tibet from 打箭鑪 Daqianlu, and arrived at Lari in December. The Dalai Lama mobilized Tibetan troops from Lhasa to 江達 Jiangda to set up defenses against the Han soldiers. He sent a letter inviting the Panchen Lama to send troops, but the Panchen Lama refused. After the Sichuan army attacked with infantry and artillery, the Tibetan troops could not hold out and retreated, pursued to 烏斯江 Wusijiang, five miles from Lhasa. At that time, Zhang Hongsheng, a committee member accompanying the army, borrowed dozens of infantrymen and took a shortcut to Lhasa, where he shot and killed a living Buddha in the crowd in the streets, and injured two or three people. The Tibetans were terrified and in a panic. The Dalai Lama, seeing this, was alarmed and asked the deputy minister Wen Zongyao to go up the mountain to request three conditions: to effectively protect the people, temples, and the Yellow Sect. Wen said that this was the original responsibility of the Han soldiers entering Tibet, and there was no need to set conditions. The Dalai Lama insisted, and Wen then consulted with Lian Yu. Unexpectedly, Lian Yu did not agree to the request. The Dalai Lama then led 虾渣卡弄 Xia Zha Ka Nong and others, going west along the river. When they were about to reach 錯木 Cuomu, a British military officer urgently telegraphed the London government, and received a reply instructing them to protect them properly and send them to Darjeeling as soon as possible. The Governor-General of India provided accommodation and other support. At that time, Chinese troops were stationed near Lhasa, and Lian Yu established military preparation and staff departments at the embassy, ​​no different from the governors of various provinces, and transferred Luo Changlu to succeed Zhong Ying as commander, accusing his soldiers of revolution every day. The soldiers were resentful. By the spring of the first year of the Republic of China, the Republic of China was established, and Commander Luo was killed in 工部 Gongbu in Tibet, and Lian Yu was also expelled. Zhong Ying appointed himself as the chief of affairs and commander. Because of his poor command of the soldiers, he aroused the anger of the Tibetans, who, under the orders of the Dalai Lama, cut off the Han soldiers' and merchants' food and salaries for more than a month. The Panchen Lama, taking pity on them, not only provided relief himself, but also secretly ordered the 第穆佛寺 Dimu Monastery and 布賚綳寺 Bulai Beng Monastery to provide relief successively. In the second year of the Republic of China, Xie Guoliang, the battalion commander of the Tu army, colluded with Tibet to attack Sichuan. The Sichuan army was about to be defeated, and after mediation by Nepal and representatives of the Panchen Lama, the Han soldiers surrendered their weapons. Later, the Gurkha company advanced funds to send the Han soldiers and merchants back to Shanghai from India. The Dalai Lama then returned to Tibet in October of the second year. The Tibetans sent troops to the Sichuan border, cutting off the eastern route and not allowing Han people to travel back and forth. Tibet continued to invade the east, and by the eighth and ninth years of the Republic of China, the Tibetan troops had occupied Ganzi on the Sichuan border, and seven or eight out of ten of all border areas had been lost. They deeply resented the Panchen Lama for providing food to the Sichuan army, and massacred all five hundred lamas of the 第穆佛寺 Dimu Monastery, burning down the temple. They also ordered the ten thousand lamas of the 布賚綳寺 Bulai Beng Monastery to collectively apologize. The monastery sent more than twenty representatives to Lhasa, where they were all subjected to torture. The discord between the Panchen Lama and the Dalai Lama arose from this. In the third year of the Republic of China, the Dalai Lama intended to seek independence, ceding the 錯那 Cuona area of Tibet to Britain, telegraphed the British government requesting its approval for independence, and asked it to send personnel to jointly resolve the pending issues between Britain and Tibet. The Chinese government sent Chen Yifan to the 赤姆納 Chimuna area in India to meet with the Dalai Lama, requesting independence, but Chen refused. The British then mediated, and designated the Lhasa, 洗自, and 槍駝 areas bordering Britain as Outer Tibet, and the 巴塘 Batang, 裏塘 Litang, and 塔多 areas bordering 西康 Xikang as Inner Tibet, and signed eight articles of agreement. The Panchen Lama, upon learning of this, feared that once the agreement was signed, national sovereignty and territory would be lost, and immediately telegraphed the chief of affairs stationed in Tibet, who forwarded the telegram to the government, and Chen was recalled. This matter was then shelved. Later, the Dalai Lama sent people to demand two million taels of silver and five hundred thousand shi of highland barley from rear Tibet every year. The Panchen Lama reluctantly agreed. Since the withdrawal of the Sichuan army from Tibetan territory, the Dalai Lama dispatched troops to garrison rear Tibet, occupying all the areas with abundant production. The military discipline was poor, and conscription was imposed on households, with all military uniforms and salaries borne by the conscripts. The people were resentful, and jointly requested the Panchen Lama to go to the mainland and seek relief from the central government. The Panchen Lama agreed. The Dalai Lama, upon hearing this news, invited the Panchen Lama to front Tibet to discuss resisting China, and threatened to resolve the matter with force if he disagreed. Fortunately, one of those involved in the discussion, a believer in the Panchen Lama, secretly reported the situation and advised him to leave quickly. The Panchen Lama then, in the eleventh month of the twelfth year of the Republic of China, lightly armed and with a reduced entourage, ventured out of Tibet. The Dalai Lama sent troops to pursue him, but the Tibetan troops deliberately moved slowly, so he was able to escape. The Panchen Lama arrived in Gansu and immediately sent a letter to the Dalai Lama, requesting him to send representatives to the central government to discuss Tibetan affairs, but received no reply. After arriving in Beiping, he again sent a trusted confidant of the Dalai Lama stationed in Beiping with a letter urging the Dalai Lama to lean towards the motherland, but again received no reply. The Panchen Lama has been in the mainland for nine years, and the government, due to the unresolved military affairs in the mainland, has not yet had a definite solution. Now, on the occasion of the National Assembly and the upcoming Tibetan Conference, all Chinese people should pay attention to the territorial and administrative relations of Tibet, and unanimously urge the government to resolve Tibetan affairs as soon as possible, which is the most urgent task of the day.

Japanese Monopolize North China Shipping 84

Newly Built Four Ships Will Extend Routes to South China

Qingdao Correspondence: Qingdao is the only trading port in central China, with convenient shipping routes to Shanghai in the south and Yantai, Weihaiwei, Tianjin, and Dalian in the north. The most prosperous route is the Shanghai-Dalian line, which is exclusively operated by the Dalian Steamship Company, a Japanese company. The Shanghai-Qingdao line is operated by China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, 太古 Taikoo, 怡和 Jardine Matheson, and 三家 Sanjia. The Qingdao-Dalian route is operated by 政記公司 Zhengji Company. The ships of the Dalian Steamship Company operate on a regular schedule and are punctual, with large tonnage and high speed. Therefore, although the fares are high, the number of passengers does not decrease. The ships of this company operating between Shanghai and Dalian include 大連丸 Dalian Maru, 奉天丸 Fengtian Maru, and 長春丸 Changchun Maru, each of which is 4,500 tons. They sail on average once every three days. The fare from Qingdao to Shanghai is 70 yuan for first class, 50 yuan for second class, and 17 yuan for third class, and the journey takes 27 hours. The fare from Qingdao to Dalian is 50 yuan for first class, 35 yuan for second class, and 12 yuan for third class. This company was originally an affiliated agency of the South Manchuria Railway Company, specializing in attracting passengers and goods for the South Manchuria Railway. Gradually, it expanded and became the only shipping agency monopolizing China's coastal shipping. It is now reported that this company has even greater ambitions and will make every effort to expand shipping. Recently, it built four new ships, one of which is the 山東丸 Shandong Maru, about 4,500 tons, built by the 玉造 Shipyard in Okayama Prefecture, managed by 三井 Mitsui, and launched on the 15th of last month. The second is the 河北丸 Hebei Maru, also 4,500 tons, built by the Nagasaki Mitsubishi Shipyard, and launched on the 20th of last month. It will be completed and put into operation on the shipping routes this year. In addition, the 山西丸 Shanxi Maru and 河南丸 Henan Maru, both 4,500 tons, are also planned to be built. The company's predetermined plan is that once these four ships are completed in the future, they will extend the routes to South China, intending to completely seize the passenger and cargo transportation of 政記 Zhengji, 招商 China Merchants, 太古 Taikoo, and 怡和 Jardine Matheson, and attract customers with low prices. If this plan is realized, China's shipping industry will suffer a more significant blow. (May 10)

Qingdao Citizens Demand Cancellation of Rent Rights 85

Clash Between Citizens and Security Team

City Authorities Agree to Temporarily Postpone Payment

Qingdao Correspondence: Previously, the citizens of Qingdao repeatedly sent representatives to the city authorities to request the cancellation of the additional rent rights levied by the municipal government, but without result. Now, the Finance Bureau has ordered the landlords to pay the rent rights within ten days, otherwise they will be detained. The landlords, under urgent circumstances, convened a general meeting at the 齊燕會館 Qi Yan Guild Hall on the 11th, with more than 400 people attending. It was decided to send the entire group to the Party and government to petition. They first went to the City 指委會 Steering Committee,

Page 10

And elected Han Jiangshi, Mou Ziming, and Ye Yujie as representatives to meet with Wu Zunming, the Minister of Propaganda, and explained their intentions. Wu said that since it concerned the pain of the masses, the City Party Department would naturally find ways to help them eliminate it. The representatives left satisfied and went to the municipal government to petition. Because of the large number of people, the city authorities specially dispatched a small team of security forces to maintain order, and sent Yu Jinhe, the Director of the Public Security Bureau, to ask the petitioners to elect representatives for contact. However, the petitioners, considering that the 40 people previously elected as representatives had negotiated several times without any effect, stated that they were willing to meet with the authorities as a whole, and the group surged towards the gate. However, the security team tried their best to stop them, and a conflict arose between the two sides, and the order was disrupted for a time. The glass of the city government gate was also broken in the melee. As a result, three of the petitioners were seriously injured, including one named Wang Qinzhai, who was unconscious at the time, and more than 20 people were slightly injured. Several police officers were also injured. At the time, petitioners Zhou Ye, Jiao Jizong, Ye Yujie, Wang Zhaolin, and Mou Ziming re-entered the city government to meet with Hu Jiafeng, the Secretary-General, and explained that this petition was originally intended to be peaceful, but unexpectedly a violent incident occurred, causing injuries to many people, which they regretted very much. Secretary-General Hu also personally went to the outside of the city government gate to comfort the masses, saying that he was acting as mayor and that everything still needed to be reported to the mayor for approval, and a reply would be given within a week. The deadline for collecting the rent rights would be postponed for ten days. Therefore, the petitioners returned to the City Chamber of Commerce to discuss measures and decided to elect 90 representatives to be responsible for negotiating the following matters with the Party and government authorities on the 12th: (1) Cancel the rent rights; (2) Punish the police officers who used weapons to injure people; (3) Provide compensation to the injured masses. If there is no result, the City Chamber of Commerce will convene a citizens' meeting and send telegrams to the government and Party departments in various places for assistance. (May 12)

New Road Protection Measures Established for the Shenhai Railway 86

Recently, banditry has been rampant in Northeast China, and cases of robbery and theft of vehicles have been frequently reported. Since the Pingji Railway opened to traffic, the Shenhai Railway has suddenly become an important transportation artery, and the number of travelers has increased day by day. However, the entire line extends for more than 250 kilometers, and the mountains and forests it passes through are complex, often frequented by bandits, and the police force is weak, making it difficult to provide comprehensive protection. Therefore, Chinese and foreign travelers are all wary. The railway authorities, therefore, submitted a request to the Liaoning Provincial Government and directly consulted with the Garrison Commander of Eastern Border to discuss measures to protect the line and passenger trains, and drafted twelve articles of service rules for the road protection army, which were submitted to the Northeast Frontier Defense Commander's Office for approval and implementation. In order to protect the line and defend local security, the Garrison Commander of Eastern Border also drew troops from the original jurisdiction and reorganized them into the First and Second Road Protection Army teams, and three independent detachments, and drafted thirteen articles of temporary regulations for the Road Protection Army, which were submitted to the Commander's Office for approval and forwarded to the Shenhai Railway for information. The service rules for the Shenhai Railway Road Protection Army are listed below: Article 1: In order to ensure the safety of passengers, this company requested the Liaoning Provincial Government to send 320 officers and soldiers from the Eastern Border Garrison Commander's Office to station along the line and patrol the line at any time to ensure security. Article 2: The places where the road protection army is stationed are listed below: Fushun, Yingpan, Cangshi, Beisanjia, Qingyuan, Yinge Men, Caoshi, Shanchengzhen, Meihekou, Hailong, Chaoyangzhen, Dongfeng, Xi'an. Article 3: The items and office buildings, coal, etc. required by the road protection army shall be supplied by the company, and the number shall be determined separately. A monthly subsidy of 2,000 yuan in silver shall be provided for the food expenses of the officers and soldiers, and all other expenses shall be borne by the army itself. Article 4: The official ranks, names, and number of officers and soldiers of the road protection army in each place shall be listed by the officers in charge and sent to the company for record. The same shall apply in case of replacement. Article 5: The road protection army should patrol the line every day, paying special attention to the following: (1) Whether there are bandits gathering near the railway, they must be strictly investigated and guarded against at any time; (2) If there are pedestrians walking on the roadbed, they should be strictly prohibited; (3) If the rails and mountain caves and bridges are destroyed or obstructed by bandits, they should immediately indicate a danger signal to stop the oncoming train and inform the workers to quickly rectify them; (4) If there are thieves or those who damage railway accessory items and electric wires and poles, they should be immediately apprehended and sent to the office for investigation. Article 6: The road protection army shall abide by all the rules of this road. Article 7: All members of the road protection army must wear specially made armbands to show identification. The style of the armband will be determined separately. Article 8: The road protection army is solely for the protection of the safety of the railway, and shall not interfere with the convenience of passengers and the handling of railway operations, unless required by the responsible personnel of the railway at all locations. Article 9: The road protection army, in addition to being subject to the orders of its superiors, must also obey the orders of the company when necessary, in order to achieve effective coordination. Article 10: The railway may, when necessary, request the garrison to withdraw the original defense or add personnel at any time. Article 11: These rules shall take effect from the date of approval. Article 12: These rules may be amended at any time if there are any omissions.

Suzhou Representatives Petition for Dredging of the Upstream Waterway of the Songkou 87

Su merchants Li Shengbo, Qian Sunqing, Yu Xiaochuan, Wang Jingting, Lan Bohua, Zhang Shouyi and other representatives of the National Assembly have made concrete plans for dredging the upstream Yangtze River waterway of the Songkou in order to maintain the prosperity of Shanghai, and have formulated reasons and methods. Yesterday (the 13th), they submitted petitions to the National Government, the Ministry of Communications, and the Yangtze River Waterway Regulation Commission. Cai Pei, the director of the Shipping Administration Department of the Ministry of Communications, agreed to report to the National Government and earnestly proceed. The reasons and methods are recorded below: (A) Reasons: Shanghai is the third most prosperous city in the world, and it will not be difficult to advance to second and first place in the future. However, because it is located at the mouth of the world's fifth largest river, the Yangtze River, it has a close relationship with water conservancy. In the past, it dredged the Huangpu River, but now it is banning pontoons. Recently, it has been excavating the 神灘 Shentan sandbar, which will make it difficult for foreign warships to navigate. The disadvantages of the mud-filling標 have already been seen. Water management must focus on the upstream. Adjusting the flow center, narrowing the width, gathering volume, and enhancing power will cause silt to move away without excavation, and fertile land will be reclaimed without cultivation. Now, from Jiangyin to the east, to the Songkou, follow this approach to make the water flow have a track to follow, and permanently cut the south side. Then, near the 白茅沙 Baimao sandbar, we can even open the night navigation ban for the first time, and the annual cost of four or five million yuan to excavate the Shentan sandbar, which is not necessarily effective, can also be opened without dredging. The convenience for shipping and the development of the economy are immeasurable. (B) Methods: (1) In terms of technology, the regulation of the Yangtze River from Jiangyin to the Songkou is a huge project, and precise measurement should be carried out first to study the required width of this section of the Yangtze River, and the degree to which the water force should be increased to wash away the Shentan sandbar, so as not to obstruct navigation. It is proposed to ask the government to instruct the Yangtze River competent authorities to study in detail, design carefully, and formulate a whole plan and budget for implementation. (2) In terms of funding, (1) follow the precedent of the 沾𤀹

The dredging tax has already been established as a precedent, and the customs will collect the dredging tax; (2) transfer the special funds for the dredging of the Shentan sandbar by the Dredging Bureau to expand the scope and engage in fundamental regulation; (3) the newly formed sand fields along the river should be commuted by the government; (4) one-third of the total allocation of the Geng indemnity should be allocated to water conservancy, and a portion should be allocated to offset the cost, following the example of guiding the Huai River and regulating the Yellow River.

Fire in Caitang Lane, Beitang: Qin Cainan, a resident of Caitang Lane, Beitang, outside the North Gate of Wuxi, works in a foreign firm in Shanghai and has saved a considerable sum. Yesterday morning (the 13th), at around 1:00 AM, a fire broke out due to negligence. Thick smoke billowed, and flames shot out in all directions, making it impossible to approach. Soon, the fire broke through the roof. The Qin family, comprising over ten men, women, and children, were all asleep. Hearing the fire alarm, they quickly put on their clothes, got out of bed, and rushed to the roof to escape, thus avoiding disaster. Fire brigades from various sections rushed to the scene with fire engines and made every effort to extinguish the blaze. After more than an hour, the fire gradually died down. Pawnshop Employee Flees with Stolen Jewelry: Li Erguan's son, Shusheng, also known as Xingbao, a resident of Henan Street, Zhangjing Bridge Town, Seventh District (Huai Shang City), has been working at the Tongji Pawnshop in Yanjia Bridge, Eighth District (Huai Xia City), for more than twenty years. Around 6:00 AM the next morning, Shusheng told the boatman Aju that he had important business today and would take the early bus to Changzhou to visit friends, and then went ashore. However, the pawnshop initially was unaware. It was not until the day before yesterday, when they were putting away the pawned gold jewelry, that they suddenly found the safe empty. Young Woman Commits Suicide Due to Prolonged Illness: Lu Asheng, a native of Ningbo, worked as a coppersmith. Several years ago, he became involved with a woman from his hometown named Wang Jinmei (29 years old), and they lived together as if they were husband and wife. Asheng then opened the Yanshengxiang Copper and Tinware Shop next to the Postal Bureau on Hanchang Road outside the Guangfu Gate. Later, Jinmei gave birth to a daughter (now five years old). Recently, Asheng, seeing that Jinmei's illness was terminal, found a young woman from Henglin as a replacement wife and built a separate house for her. When Jinmei found out about this, she was deeply dissatisfied and contemplated suicide. On the evening of the 7th of this month, she secretly took four red pills in an attempt to end her life. Fortunately, her partner noticed and rushed her to the Tongren Hospital for treatment, saving her life. The day before yesterday, Jinmei took advantage of the lack of attention, found a pair of sharp scissors in the room, and stabbed her throat several times. Blood gushed out, and she collapsed to the ground, barely breathing and unconscious. Lu Asheng found out about this and immediately sent her to the Brothers Hospital for treatment. However, due to excessive blood loss, the treatment was ineffective. She passed away yesterday morning around 10:00 AM.

Yangzhong 95

Commits Suicide by Poisoning After Unable to Recover Debt: Wu Kunlong, a worker in the Yangzhong County Party Department, was naturally timid. Through years of hard work, he had saved a little money. Ji Zhiy, a neighbor who ran a sesame seed cake shop, coveted his wealth and pretended to be friendly, tricking him into depositing 180 yuan of his savings in the shop. In February of this year, Wu Kunlong quarreled with Ji Zhiy over his inability to withdraw his deposit. Tang Jisheng, a member of the Party Committee, Liu Yulin, the principal of Sanmao Elementary School, and Zhu Jinzhang and other neighbors mediated, and Ji Zhiy transferred two mu of land to Wu Kunlong for management, with a written agreement, and the matter was resolved. Afterwards, the relationship between the two men was erratic, with occasional visits and inquiries, but quarrels and disputes were almost daily occurrences, leaving everyone baffled. On the evening of the 9th, Wu Kunlong argued with Ji Zhiy again because he could not recover the money for the flour he had purchased. On the morning of the 10th, Ji instigated his wife to rush to the entrance of the Party Department, grab Wu Kunlong, and curse and scold him on the ground. The First Public Security Branch sent police to arrest both parties and released them on bail shortly after. Wu Kunlong, feeling humiliated and resentful after being unable to recover his debt and being insulted, contemplated suicide. He secretly went to a smoking den and purchased one yuan of raw opium, sitting in the sesame seed cake shop. In the evening, the poison took effect, and his face turned pale. The shop owner, Ji Zhiy, and his wife, seeing that they had caused trouble, took the opportunity to escape. Neighbors hired a doctor to treat him, but the poisoning was too deep, and the treatment was ineffective. He died around 11:00 PM that night. The landlord, surnamed Zhu, fearing being implicated, reported it to the Public Security Branch, which sent police to the countryside and arrested the culprit, Ji Zhiy, in a small widow's house near Shisiwei and sent him to the county government for detention. It is reported that on the 12th, the news was transmitted to the family of the deceased, who sent personnel to examine the body. The Party Department has sent a letter to the county government requesting that it be handled according to law.

The Coastal Protection and Bandit Suppression Process in Jiangsu Province: In March, the Jiangsu Provincial Government convened a provincial conference on the protection of the fishing industry. Representatives of the fishing industry along the coast of northern Jiangsu described the brutal situation of the sea bandits. The provincial government, together with the Provincial Pacification Supervisor and the National Coast Guard Department of the Navy Department, handled the protection of the fishing industry and bandit suppression. Because bandit spies were densely distributed in various parts of northern Jiangsu, they secretly discussed a plan of action in the province, Shanghai and other places. On the one hand, the province ordered the county government to find ten pilots from Lusi to Doulonggang in Yancheng, hire more than thirty sea boats, and establish a temporary office for coastal protection of Jiangsu along the coast of Tongcheng. Ding Zhennan, director of the Coast Guard Department, was appointed as director, and Zhang Han, director of the Wusong Water Police District, and Pan Taowan, head of the 282nd Regiment, were appointed as deputy directors. Seven radio stations were set up along the coast. Once the deployment was completed, Directors Zhang and Pan led military police ships to Lusi to suppress the bandits. There were more than forty patrol boats and warships. The bandit ships were approximately thirty. The bandits only paid attention to the military police in the south. They did not expect the interception in the north. Many people were killed and injured. Outside Huanhai Port, a bandit ship was captured. There were only eight bandit corpses and three guns on board. Many other bandit ships were destroyed by artillery fire. More than twenty fishing boats and eighty crew members that were kidnapped by the bandits have all escaped and returned. The Tonghai, Ruyang and Qi oceans have been completely pacified. Among the bandits, Shen Fengshan, a force of 500 men, surrendered to the government troops. With the approval of the provincial government, the Security Department reorganized them into the Jiangsu Maritime Guerrilla Force. This team, assisted by artillery sent by the military police, was extremely effective in the suppression. Many people died in the Battle of Juegang. The remaining three hundred or so have reached Dongtai Pincha and are joining forces with the Huaibei Maritime Police Guerrilla Force to pursue the fleeing bandits to the north.

Ningbo 97

Son Arrests Father for Adultery, Requests Clan Chief to Decide: Chen Ensheng, from Chen Gongling, Fenghua, inherited a large amount of ancestral property. Later, because Ensheng indulged in evil habits and gambling, he spent a lot of money, leading to the decline of his family. At first, he pawned clothes and jewelry, then sold fields and houses. His son, Zenghe, initially endured it, then complained. Recently, a major conflict broke out. His father, Ensheng, hating his son for being unfilial, discussed with his mistress, Chen Yinge, planning to send Zenghe to the authorities for investigation. However, his son found out about it. That night, he gathered more than ten clan members and caught his father in adultery at midnight, dragging Yinge and his father, Ensheng, out of bed, tying them up, and sending them to the ancestral hall, requesting the clan chief to decide. The outcome is unknown.

Bengbu 98

Lieshan Labor Strike to Be Resolved Soon: The Lieshan Coal Mine in Su County experienced twists and turns when Li Battalion of the 39th Regiment of the 7th Division stationed in Suixi arrested bandits, which triggered a strike by all coal mine workers. Details were reported in previous newspapers. It is now learned that after Lu Zidong, the general manager of the mine, arrived in Xuzhou, he originally intended to meet with Division Commander Wang Jun face-to-face to negotiate. Because Wang went to Beijing, his chief of staff met with him instead. Lu reported the course of events and requested that he be instructed to quickly release Xu Ziqin, the supervisor of the mine workers, and the thirty or so workers who had been arrested, in order to resume work and avoid long-term losses to the mine. Wang's chief of staff agreed to instruct Li Battalion to release them as soon as possible to resume work. Lu then went to Lieshan to inspect. According to current observations, the Lieshan incident can be resolved peacefully within a few days. Once the workers are released and the mine resumes work, Lu Zidong will return to Bengbu.

Letter from Huang Zhifang 99

To the Editor: I have just read a report in the Jiangyin Correspondence column of your newspaper on May 11, stating that the market strike in Houteng has temporarily ended, which is inconsistent with the facts. In this case, my director did not privately torture Zhu Xianghan or apologize to the merchants of Houteng by setting off firecrackers. The facts are all there and cannot be concealed. This concerns credibility, and I am deeply afraid of causing confusion. I am sending this special letter to correct it. Please publish it. Huang Zhifang, Director of the Third Branch of the Jiangyin County Public Security Bureau, May 11

Education News, This City

Municipal Education Bureau Cracks Down on Unqualified Private Schools 100

Zuoxin Elementary School

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau sent a letter to the Municipal Public Security Bureau yesterday, stating that it had received repeated complaints from citizens Zhu Nancheng and Zhang Yelu about Shi Jiucheng, the principal and teacher of the private Zuoxin Elementary School at 1312 Dongzishou Lane, Qiujiang Road, Zhabei District, lacking academic qualifications and also holding positions as a doctor and lawyer. The school was a single room, serving as both a school and a doctor's office, and a law firm. It was misleading children and requested a strict crackdown. An investigation confirmed that there were indeed doctor and lawyer signs hanging at the school entrance. The interior was sparsely equipped, like a private school. The allegations made by Zhu Nancheng and others were not without evidence and should be strictly suppressed to avoid misleading children. In addition to the approval, a letter was sent requesting investigation and suppression.

Mathematics Conference of Secondary Schools in Jiangsu Province 101

In order to improve efficiency, Jiangsu Province's secondary schools have successively held subject conferences on Chinese, English, Party Affairs, and other subjects. The Shanghai Provincial High School was responsible for convening a mathematics conference for middle schools throughout the province, which commenced at 10 AM the day before yesterday (the 11th). Shen Yizhen chaired the meeting, Wang Gangsen recorded, and Zheng Xigu, the principal of Shanghai High School, delivered a speech. Wu Zaiyuan, a mathematics expert, lectured, elaborating on the teaching materials and key teaching points of mathematics for high school and junior high school. After the lecture, the charter and proposals were discussed. More than a dozen proposals were approved, the most valuable of which was to seek a common standard for mathematics courses in high school and junior high school.

China Vocational Education Society Promotes Design Committee 102

Various middle schools have requested design services.

The China Vocational Education Society's Design Committee held its first meeting yesterday. Those present were Huang Renzhi, Pan Yangyao, Liu Zhansi, Shen Youqian, Liu Tuling, Wang Qihua, Huang Puqi, Zhao Yuwu, Chen Xuanzhao, Yao Huiquan, Wang Zizhu, Wang Hengyuan, Wu Cuilun, and Yang Weiyu. Liu Zhanen was elected as chairman, Chen Qingshi as vice chairman, and Wu Cuilun as recorder. After performing the customary ceremonies, the following resolutions were made: (1) The proposal to revise the Vocational Education Implementation Guidelines published by the Society was approved. Everyone will sign and submit their notes to the director, vice director, chairman, and vice chairman by the end of the month. (2) The proposal to add a teacher training program to the China Vocational School was approved. Zhao Yuwu explained the purpose of the proposal and the outline of the plan, which was approved. At this point, the chairman withdrew and was succeeded by Chen Qingshi. (3) The proposal from Jiangdu County Junior High School requesting guidance on reorganization was approved. Yao Huiquan will be asked to investigate in Jiangdu first. (4) The proposal from Haimen Private Jinming Vocational School requesting guidance on planning was approved. Wang Qihua will be asked to review it. (5) The proposal from Yixing County High School requesting amendment of the plan was approved. Huang Renzhi, Yang Weiyu, and Wang Qihua will be asked to review it. (6) The proposal regarding the date of the regular meeting of the association was approved. It was decided to temporarily change it to once a month, with the date to be determined by the administrative department. (7) The proposal to organize a vocational education travel research group was approved. The administrative department will plan and organize it. (8) The Shanghai Fruit Industry Private Huashi Elementary School sent a letter requesting help in hiring a vocational supplementary course teacher and revising the articles of association. In addition to the guidance office recommending a teacher, the name can be changed to Vocational Course, and courses such as cultivation, preservation, and decoration can be added. Graduates must serve for a certain period of time before being issued a certificate. The above points will be communicated by Huang Renzhi, and the meeting adjourned.

Fudan Law School Invites Zhang Yuanruo to Lecture 103

—The Many Aspects of the Constitutional Law Problem—

In order to enliven the lecture hall life, the Department of Politics of Fudan University Law School recently organized a lecture society, inviting famous scholars from the country to give academic lectures. The first lecture was held yesterday, with four to five hundred attendees. The speaker was Zhang Yuanruo, former professor of the Law School of Central University and current president of the School of Social Sciences of the National Labor University, who spoke on the topic of the many aspects of the constitutional law problem. It was divided into three parts: (1) Why do we need a constitutional law? (2) What kind of constitutional law do we need? (3) How should we formulate a constitutional law? He elaborated based on academic principles, and the lecture lasted for two hours.

Jiangnan University Basketball Tournament: Chih Tze Wins Championship 104

Achieving Seven Wins in Seven Games

Defeated Jiaotong University Yesterday 51 to 25

The Chih Tze University basketball team has many talented players and has been training for a long time. They have achieved outstanding results in various competitions this season. In this basketball championship organized by the Jiangnan University Sports Association, a total of eight schools participated. Chih Tze has won seven games and has successfully won this year's championship.

Yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM, Chih Tze played its last game against Jiaotong University in Xujiahui. Although Jiaotong University has some skills, it was no match for the well-organized Chih Tze. As a result, Chih Tze won 51 to 25. The referee was Gong Zhenyi.

The game began, and neither side scored within the first three minutes. Then, because Chih Tze committed a foul, Jiaotong University took the lead in opening the score. Both sides attacked and defended, and the situation was quite tense. Later, the score reached 3 to 3. But from then on, Chih Tze's momentum grew, and they went on to win the first half 18 to 9. In the second half, the situation remained the same. Jiaotong University tried to retaliate and was also very aggressive, but due to slightly inferior skills, they could not turn the tide. Chih Tze then triumphed with a score of 51 to 25.

Excellent Track and Field Results in Shandong 110

Shot Put Breaks National Record

Women's 100m Hurdles Also Good

Jinan Correspondence, 10th: The Shandong Provincial Games began at 9:00 AM. Zhang Suhui, a competitor from Women's Middle School No. 1, was the individual all-around champion in the junior division at the first Provincial Games, gaining fame throughout the province and earning the title of Shandong's Sun Guiyun. Therefore, both the athletes and the spectators were eager to witness her performance. As expected, she lived up to her reputation. In the preliminary round of the women's 100-meter dash, Ms. Zhang broke her own record of 16 1/5 seconds from the first National Games with a time of 15 seconds. In the preliminary round of the 50-meter dash, she broke the North China record of 8 seconds with a time of 5 4/5 seconds. Her rapid progress is truly astonishing. In the men's division, Yang Xuexian of the Qilu Sports Association (organized by students of Qilu University in Jinan) broke the national record of 108 feet from last year with a shot put of 33.40 meters and broke the North China record of 5.80 meters held by Huang Kai'ao from the 14th Games with a long jump of 5.82 meters. In the women's eight-pound shot put, Liu Yulan of No. 2 Normal School broke the North China record of 7.82 meters held by Hu Chunli from the 14th Games with a throw of 7.94 meters. According to last year's national record of 108 feet for the shot put, which is equivalent to 31.87 meters and was set by Zhao Wenzao, Yang Xuexian was able to surpass it. Yang, whose given name is Ji Chao, is from Tai'an, Shandong, and is 27 years old. He served as the Director of Studies at the Tai'an English Middle School for two years and is currently a freshman in the Faculty of Arts and Science at Qilu University in this city.

The 11th was the second day of the Provincial Games, and approximately 20,000 people attended. In the women's 80-meter hurdles, Yu Xiulan, a student from the Provincial Fourth Normal School, broke the records of 16.8 seconds from Harbin and 16.5 seconds from Tianjin with a time of 16.1 seconds. Yu is 18 years old and is from Linqu County in this province. She is a sophomore in the pre-course program at Qingdao 34th Normal School. In the women's 50-meter dash, Zhang Suhui, a student from Women's Middle School, burst into tears because she released [her starting block] too early and ran off course. However, in the women's 200-meter dash, Zhang (Suhui) later broke the record of 31.4 seconds held by Peng Jingbo, an athlete from Harbin at the 14th North China Games, with a time of 31 seconds. Record of the Liangjiang Girls' School Basketball Team's Eastern Expedition (Sent from Osaka by Huang Jiping) 111

—Lost to Pharmacy School 19 to 20—Defeated Kansai 30 to 10

Unfortunately Lost to Pharmacy School

(Osaka Communication, 7th) The Liangjiang Girls' School basketball team arrived in Osaka at noon on the 6th. The players were extremely exhausted due to the long journey. They originally planned to rest for a while before competing with various teams, but the Osaka and Kansai Basketball Associations had already scheduled the matches and could not reschedule. The Liangjiang players had no choice but to do their best, even playing while feeling unwell, regardless of the outcome. Thus, they played against the Imperial Pharmacy School team at the YMCA field at 5:30 PM on the 7th. Mr. Isawa and Mr. Sawada served as referees. Liangjiang performed well in the first quarter, but their strength declined, and their performance did not improve. Repeated fouls were also a contributing factor. Seeing an opportunity, the Pharmacy School team pushed forward and scored more points in the second and third quarters. The fourth quarter was a tie. As a result, Liangjiang lost by a score of 20 to 19. Osaka newspapers reported on the game the next day, saying that it was a "glorious defeat." In terms of skill, Liangjiang performed admirably, but they were ultimately unable to win due to fatigue. The score sheet is as follows:

Free Talk

World Tidbits 112

—Seagull

There are as many as eleven varieties of pigs produced in England, all of which are excellent. Among European countries, only Denmark can be considered a strong rival to English pig production, because they have discovered a particularly good breed of pig that is unmatched by England.

A large number of French soldiers died in the European War. A rose bush is planted on the grave of each soldier as a marker.

London has a state-of-the-art hospital where patients can simply press a button on their bedside to move the mattress, allowing them to sit up or lie down comfortably, as they wish.

Canada produces so many chicken eggs that there is a "Eat More Eggs" campaign to increase the average annual consumption of chicken eggs to 125 per person.

The British House of Commons is the most famous legislative building in the world. It is extremely large, with 1,000 rooms.

Multiple small log cabins have been newly built in the forests near Berlin, Germany, to serve as temporary chapels for worship by visitors on Sundays.

Wedding rings are traditionally worn on the fourth finger of the left hand. However, many American and British women have changed their practice and now wear them on the third finger of the right hand.

Eight-Fingered Ascetic 113

—Jielu

While reading Linghua Jun's travelogue of India in "Free Talk," Daojie Fashi is often mentioned. This reminds me of his master, the Eight-Fingered Ascetic, which shows that there are many eminent monks in Buddhism. The ascetic's Dharma name is Jing'an, and he calls himself Jichan. He was from Hunan. He lost his parents at a young age and became a monk at a temple in Hengshan due to poverty. He was assigned to the task of feeding the cats and dogs. One day, he saw peach blossoms falling from the fence, covering the stream with red petals, and suddenly had an epiphany. He then burned two fingers in front of the Buddha. Unknowingly, his wisdom greatly increased. He visited Yueyang Tower and saw the vast expanse of Dongting Lake, and spontaneously recited, "Dongting waves send a monk here." From then on, his literary talent flourished, and his writing was elegant and refined. Scholars were surprised, thinking that Jia Dao had been reborn. Fan Fanshan, Yi Ku'an, Chen San'yuan, and others frequently composed and sang poetry with him. While living at Tiantong Temple in Siming, he also frequently composed poems with local elders Sheng Shengchuan and Chen Tianying. The Eight-Fingered Ascetic's Poetry Collection, which he published, is said to rival the Tang Dynasty poems. The Master was a burly man with a booming voice. His study of Buddhism seems less profound than Dixian of the Tiantai school or as novel as Taixu, but the Ascetic was forthright and honest, and he was deeply patriotic and righteous. He did not discuss Buddhist doctrine, but he was deeply aligned with Buddhist principles. Observing his founding of the Buddhist Association and monastic schools, his achievements were remarkable. How can we simply label him a "poet monk"? During the time when Yuan Shikai was in power, the Ascetic went to Yandu to have the Buddhist Association registered but was ridiculed by a section chief. He was very angry and passed away that evening at an inn. His disciple Daojie, the abbot of Fayuan Temple, managed his funeral and buried him in his prepared tomb at Tiantong in Siming. Plum blossoms were planted all around the tomb. It is what the Master's poem called "Transmit the mind with a bright moon, bury the bones among ten thousand plum blossoms." Now, I will record several of the Master's poems below. Bao Xie, the attendant, sent me a poem from his friend Li Shangshan Qun, mourning his female disciple Hua Yuezhen. I wrote two quatrains after it: "On the shore of Moon Lake is a house, a fifteen-year-old girl's temples are just beginning to darken. Not allowing red dust to contaminate jade bones, the wild wind blows down white lotus flowers." "Purple orchid fragrance cleanses the heavy door, recognizing the exiled soul from the heavens. Do not sing mournfully by the lake, fleeting flowers in a mirror, the moon in the water, casually leaving traces." I wrote on the poetry scroll of the Korean Kim Duitang, collected by Wang Wusheng, the director: "Wanting to sing collecting ferns in the Western Mountains, white clouds' thoughts are contrary to the times. Who will take the lonely tears of a subject from the East Sea and blow them onto the old robes of the Southern Dynasties?" "What is the regret for the country being destroyed and the body remaining? Pitying the bronze camel in the thorns. The surrendered king loves the concubines of the Wei Palace, the brave warrior sadly sings the song of the Yishui." One day after the Double Ninth Festival, I sent a message from Jinling to Wei Xuezhuo in Taihu: "Again as a visitor to Jiangnan, sadly recalling old travels. Light frost on the leaves of Dongting, the setting sun on the autumn of Moling. Asking about the Double Ninth Festival, where to climb high? A man in white should send wine, did you insert chrysanthemums?" Poetry and lyrics are the wisdom of people. The Master, with only a slight knowledge of letters, achieved so much. The Buddhist theory of the six supernatural powers is indeed not false.

Huating Cranes 114

—Gu Zhizhou

When reading the History of Jin, Lu Ji sighed when he was executed, "Will I ever hear the cranes of Huating again?" This shows that cranes from Huating County have been known since ancient times. The species still exists today. In the territory of the county, by the slopes and watersides, with scarlet crowns and white feathers, long necks and slender legs, they can often be seen, like lofty hermits visiting the stream and seeking scenic spots. They are smaller in shape than the ordinary cranes we see. Their tails and wings have no mixed feathers, and their entire bodies are pure white. The most amazing thing is that they never fly out of Huating, so they are rarely seen elsewhere. Their nests are often built on the large trees in front of the county government. They are quite docile in nature. Except for foraging for food, they often curl one leg up and close both eyes, perched on the top of the tree. Even if children shout and disturb them below, they remain with their eyes closed and legs curled. Or if someone throws a brick at them, and it does not hit them, they simply open their eyes and glance down. Their quietness and composure, unwilling to be disturbed, is such. It is truly a model for us. However, because of this, they are often harmed by archers. Although the authorities have repeatedly prohibited this, it is evident that the archers do as they please, and the orders are not followed. I have heard that Westerners not only preserve and study ancient artifacts, but they also raise and protect rare species of birds and animals, so that they may be preserved permanently. I am deeply afraid that the cranes of Huating will become extinct within a few decades, like the unicorns and phoenixes, leaving only beautiful names in the world.

Mourning Master Mei Ju 115

—Wu Jiren

Master Wang Mei Ju of Guangdong was nearly seventy years old, open-minded, and possessed the talent to save the world. Sadly, he was stuck in the literary world and not used by the world. In his prime, he was a law official, known for his integrity. In recent years, he resided in Shanghai, tutoring the two sons of Mr. Du Meishu. My friend, Cai Jun Bomin, had three generations of friendship with the Master. He thought I was a poor writer with a meager income and nowhere to learn. He introduced me to the Master. After that, every time I visited, I would ask for advice. Although the Master was old, he was vigorous in spirit and explained in great detail without tiring. Every time he wrote an essay, in addition to making revisions, he would write another one for me to consult. However, due to my job at the Mingxing Film Company, which kept me busy, I was unable to follow him day and night. I only studied diligently for three months. Thinking of it now, I am filled with endless sorrow.

I was later dismissed from the company because of a disagreement with Director Song. The Master often expressed his regret and encouraged me, saying, "Be harmonious in life and upright in conduct. Do not be arrogant, and strive to maintain your personal integrity." I received his kind words and engraved them in my heart. For more than a year after leaving the Master, I was constantly thinking of him. In March of this year, I rejoined Mingxing, but I was too busy with writing to visit him. On the first day of April, I received his address from Mr. Shou Juan and went to visit him. The Master had just recovered from an illness but was still energetic and unchanged from before. We talked for two hours, and he asked me in detail about my situation after we parted. The Master once said, "Now that you have a home, you should work hard and not waste time." When he learned that I was addicted to raising goldfish, he told me to bring a few when I returned home because he had also raised them in his youth. I remember that he had an article on goldfish raising published in a certain newspaper.

The Master liked to drink, but he never refused or got drunk. In recent years, his illness recurred, and his liver energy rose frequently. He began to abstain from alcohol. I was planning to choose a day to prepare wine and food and have a good drink with the Master, but unexpectedly, the sad news came that he had been summoned to heaven. Recalling the depth of love we had shared over the years, I could not help but burst into tears. I write this to express my grief.

Entering the pavilion, I found the scenery to be ordinary and lacked charm. If Su Shunqin knew, he would probably agree with me. There is a fine arts school inside, headed by my schoolmate

Wild Game 117

— Lou Lou

People in the South primarily eat rice. Although they also occasionally consume wheat products, their choices are limited to noodles and pastries. However, people in the North have a much wider variety of wheat-based foods. These days, it is the time when "the wheat fields send a breeze carrying the fragrance of cakes and pastries." I will introduce some Yuan wheat products that are most interesting in our Jiangbei region.

Fragrant Green Wheat: Use green Yuan wheat that has matured but not yet withered and yellowed. Roast it in a pot until cooked. It's delicious.

Cold Needles: Lightly stir-fry green Yuan wheat in a pot. Then, grind it with a millstone. This will produce soft, long, needle-like strands. The taste is fresh and pleasant.

Cold Needle Pancakes: Sun-dry the cold needles and store them. You can mix them with flour and large shrimp to make pancakes. They have a unique flavor.

Wheat Flake Congee: Grind the matured wheat into fine flakes. Use them to cook congee with rice. This not only saves firewood but is also very healthy.

Coarse Wheat Rice: Grind Yuan wheat into coarse flakes. It can be cooked with rice. Eating this kind of rice in summer is very cool and refreshing.

Around the Yellow Sea (II) 118

— Huang Yanpei

On the 20th, we arrived in Qingdao and stopped for four hours. We visited the old German artillery battery, Qingdao University, and the observatory.

The Qingdao University campus was formerly the Bismarck Barracks. It opened last year with two colleges: Liberal Arts and Sciences. The College of Liberal Arts is divided into three departments: Chinese Philosophy, Foreign Philosophy, and Education. The College of Science is divided into four departments: Mathematics, Physics, Chemistry, and Biology. There are over a hundred students and thirty faculty members. The annual budget actually received is 360,000 yuan allocated by the province and 48,000 yuan allocated by the Jiaoji Railway, totaling 408,000 yuan.

The Qingdao Observatory was built by the Germans and later occupied by the Japanese. It was taken over by the Republic of China in 1922. It currently has departments of Meteorology, Seismology, Astronomy, Magnetism, and Oceanography. It sends out weather maps daily. During the Japanese occupation, it was limited to Japanese ships and used Japanese language. Now, it is available to both Chinese and foreign ships. It has a shortwave radio station for receiving and transmitting weather telegrams. Ships near the coast can directly inquire about storms, etc., and receive replies. For the past three years, it has used an electric time signal instead of a noon gun, three times a day, which is quite accurate. New domes and equatorial rooms have been built, and large telescopes and solar and lunar photography equipment have been purchased. The China Education and Culture Foundation Board of Directors has provided a special grant of 25,000 yuan to purchase equatorial and meridian instruments to train meteorological talent. The director, Jiang Bingran, has been in this position since the takeover and is very diligent. He publishes various charts, annual reports, monthly reports, and other publications, totaling dozens. However, the monthly expenses are only 3,000 yuan, which are paid by the municipal government.

This observatory is still a pending case between China and Japan. When it was taken over in 1922, Japan refused to relinquish its maritime academic rights in East Asia, claiming that China had no specialized personnel in this field and refused to return it. After negotiations, it was stipulated that China would send a director and trainees, but Japanese staff would continue to work and would not receive Chinese compensation. After the technicians were trained, they would be handed over to the Japanese staff. It was also agreed to establish free communication methods with various places in Japan. In reality, China was not lacking in such technicians. Later, the Japanese staff submitted a written opinion stating that China already had such technicians and that it should be completely returned. However, negotiations have stalled due to various prevarications by the Japanese side.

Rotary Club Storytelling

Hawthorne's Detective Turn (13) 119

— Cheng Xiaoqing

The question raised by Hawthorne was indeed very important. However, the situation behind the scenes was very complicated, and a proper conclusion could not be reached immediately. After more than ten minutes of consideration, we assumed three possible causes: besides theft and pranks, as Hawthorne had suggested, we also assumed an ideal of revenge. Hawthorne said, "This person's plan is very meticulous and very insidious. It is definitely not the kind of prank that ordinary friends would play. Imagine, at that time, if my old friend Bao Lang had taken another step forward, wouldn't his life have been in danger?" Zhang Baoquan nodded and said, "Yes, this matter was indeed extremely dangerous. What is most hateful is that Qiu Kui is really too stupid and useless." Hawthorne said, "If this detective's actions were truly out of stupidity, that would be excusable. Otherwise, I cannot help but suspect that he is in collusion." Zhang Baoquan quickly said, "This is definitely not the case. I can guarantee it. Tonight, I passed by the Gao family's door and saw that there were many carriages and horses outside, so I guessed that there were many guests. Therefore, in addition to following Gao Peixian's request to send four police officers to take care of things, I also sent Qiu Kui to guard in secret, to prevent any accidents. But I didn't expect him to make such a big mistake. But I decided to send him only at dusk, so collusion in advance is impossible." Hawthorne lowered his head and flicked some ash from his fingers, without answering immediately. I then interjected, "If Mr. Zhang can guarantee that he is not in collusion, that would be best. But it would be better for him to make some demonstration, so that we can trust him." Zhang Baoquan said, "How should he demonstrate? Please tell me, Mr. Bao, and I will definitely make him follow your instructions." I said, "Since the villain was let go by him at the time, he should be responsible for tracking him down and bringing him back. I think that within three days, he should hand that person over to us, or at least find out his whereabouts." Zhang Baoquan nodded repeatedly and said, "Good, good. This is not only his responsibility, but also my duty, and I should be equally responsible." Although Hawthorne did not participate in this suggestion, he clearly agreed with it. He stood up and wrapped the collar on the desk with the white cloth again. He said, "Brother Baoquan, since that's the case, let's proceed separately. I will keep this thing for now. You can agree to that, right?"

Yi Chang sold 850 bales, Yongfeng sold 700 bales, Shen Da sold 550 bales, Rongxing sold 600 bales, and Heshen bought 950 bales, Tongyu bought 650 bales, Tianlong bought 500 bales, Hengde bought 600 bales, and Deji bought 500 bales. However, spot cotton transactions were sluggish, and some retail investors shorted.

Grains 127

Foreign Rice: New Order for Over 1,400 Tons

May-June Futures... Japanese Traders Dumped... Local Dealers Purchased

Yesterday, the trading of Kehsien rice remained sluggish. Keh gangs maintained their standstill, and the general market only had 167 bags of Hunan machine-processed rice at a price of 10 yuan and 85 cents, which were purchased by local dealers. There were no other transactions.

Foreign rice has been absent from the market for a long time. The previous order was directly shipped by the Keh gangs, so there were no transactions in the market. However, yesterday, a new order for over 1,400 tons was placed by local dealers with Japanese traders, all dumped by Mitsui & Co. It includes 650 bags of No. 1 Saigon rice, to be shipped at the end of May, priced at 5 taels and 43 cents per hundred catties; and 800 tons of Small Ground rice, to be shipped in early June, priced at 5 taels and 6 cents. No. 1 Saigon rice was distributed among local dealers, while Small Ground rice was ordered by Dingfeng, Dingtai, Dafeng, Xie Daheng, Xingji, and other firms.

Silk and Tea 128

Factory Raw Silk: Telegraphic Price Fluctuations Indicate Flat or Hidden Declines

Yesterday, the local foreign firms' silk market was flat and weak. European and American silk factories were still slow to purchase Shanghai white factory raw silk due to the low price of Japanese silk. Although there were telegraphic price fluctuations from England and France, the exchange rate remained flat or showed hidden declines, making transactions difficult. Yesterday, only Lienar and others purchased 50 bales of Shanghai white factory raw silk, and Qianli purchased 50 bales of white dried raw silk. Prices did not increase.

Few Hangzhou and Shaoxing Cocoon Merchants Renew Licenses 129

Statistics Show Less Than 20-30%. Decreasing Number of Silkworm Harvests.

The silkworm season in Hangzhou and Shaoxing is the earliest, but this year the weather has been unfavorable. The early silkworms failed, and the late silkworms were affected by extreme cold and heavy rain, resulting in 50-60% losses. According to inquiries from various cocoon merchants, due to the lack of tenants, the number of those who paid and renewed their licenses was very small, statistically less than 20-30%. The silkworm industry is now facing another blow. As silkworms are being placed on racks, the number of cocoon merchants preparing to open their harvests will decrease further. The cocoon market in Zhejiang province this year is expected to be in dire straits.

Qimen and Fuliang Black Tea Harvests Face Deficits 130

The Qimen and Fuliang black tea, which has attracted much attention, was reported by a Jiujiang telegram yesterday to have already shipped over 3,000 boxes through Gutang in Jiangxi province. It is expected to arrive in Shanghai this Saturday. However, the cost of this black tea for Chinese merchants is between 200 taels and 300 yuan, an unprecedentedly high price. The reason for this is due to the deficient harvests. According to reports from Qimen and Fuliang, the production of various mountains is only 60% of last year, while the number of tea processing firms has increased by more than 30, resulting in supply shortages and excessively high tea prices.

Local New Tea Sales to Europe Are Sluggish 131

Yesterday, the foreign firms' tea market continued to be quiet. Although 100-200 boxes of green tea from Huzhou and Suian, produced by local tea factories, were available, English firms were unwilling to actively purchase them due to the high tea prices. No transactions were seen throughout the city.

Ningzhou Tea Industry Plunges 132

Ningzhou is an important tea-producing area in Jiangxi province. In recent years, sales to foreign firms have been sluggish, and the production area has been ravaged by bandits and communists. The output has decreased sharply year by year. Although the bandits and communists in the urban areas of this region have been suppressed, the remote rural areas are still unstable. As a result, tea merchants are hesitant, and only two tea processing firms remain, with limited operations due to tight credit. This year, the foreign firms' tea output in this region is no more than 4,000 boxes, indicating a sharp decline in the tea industry.

Piece Goods 133

Both Chinese and Foreign Goods Show General Stability

Local Cloth: There has been very little change in recent days. Retail sales are sporadic, mainly because it is the off-season and demand from northern ports is sluggish. Although Ningbo and Wenzhou gangs are making purchases, they are also limited. Fine twills, affected by the unrest in Guangdong, rose once but have since fallen again. Those who advanced payment for coarse cloth have been gradually withdrawing. Fortunately, Flower Yarn is still strong, so the price of goods has not weakened. Yesterday, Yanghe fine twills fell slightly, Blue Double Fish remained stable, and Squirrel was still within the 7 taels range. However, Ewo & Co. bleached cloth is increasingly scarce, reaching 8 taels and 65 cents. Fine cloth brands such as Colored Ball, Yanghe, and Trumpet Boy remain around 7 taels and 40 cents. Shipments of coarse twills are decreasing, but outbound traffic is also limited.

Eastern and Western Piece Goods: Among Eastern goods, Yuan foreign yarn is particularly strong. Point Autumn Fragrance requires 10 taels and 35 cents, fluctuating rapidly. Han Shan Temple Double Child Deer and other brands have also become stronger. Fine bombazine: yesterday, Three Friends Picture suddenly rose to 30 cents and 7.5 mils, due to the scarcity of spot goods. White crepe cloth is still difficult to rise due to the abundance of spot goods. Copper Plate remains at 4 taels, 1 mace, and 7.5 cents. Moganshan, Man and Dog, and Banana Leaf Inscribed Book brands are all at 4 taels and 1 mace. Large Swirl bombazine has softened, falling to 27.5 cents. Zhongshan flannel sales are quiet, and blue satin arrivals are increasingly abundant, making it difficult to maintain prices. Among Western goods, bleached cloth is stronger, and the brands that should be sold are lacking.

Local News

Sun Ke Issues Two Important Telegrams on the Current Situation 137

Telegram to Chairman Chiang

Telegram to Gu, Chen, etc.

Sun Ke, Minister of Railways of the National Government, has been recuperating in Shanghai for several days. The Central Government, in order to invite him to attend the National Conference, sent representatives Wu Zhihui, Zhang Jingjiang, Li Shizeng, and Kong Xiangxi to Shanghai to urge him to go to Nanjing and to mediate in the Guangdong situation. This has been reported in previous newspapers. It is now learned that Sun Ke, in order to mediate in the current situation, issued two important telegrams on the 5th and 8th of this month, one to Chiang Kai-shek, Chairman of the National Government, and the other to Gu Yingfen, Chen Jitang, and others of the Guangdong Committee. Both telegrams have been published successively. They are recorded below. Telegram to Chairman Chiang: Yesterday, Brother Tie visited Shanghai and relayed your instructions, stating that you have decided to resolve the Guangdong issue through the Party, without resorting to military or political means, and that the relationship between taxation and the Party is extremely close, and it is not appropriate to passively supervise and blame at this critical juncture. Upon hearing this, I feel deeply ashamed. I have been involved in Party affairs for nearly thirty years, and I would not hesitate to go through fire and water for the benefit of the Party and the country. I am bound by great righteousness and have no room for evasion. If I still fail to fulfill my duty to offer my suggestions to you on this matter, I would not only fail you, but also the Party and the country. I dare to respectfully submit my humble opinions to you. Since you assumed office two years ago, you have worked tirelessly day and night for the Party and the country. Your desire to assist you in completing the unfinished business of the late Premier is well known to all comrades. Differences of opinion may arise from time to time, and you may express your candid views straightforwardly, but this also stems from your love for the Party and you. If it is said that there is any intention of harboring dissent, I am sure that there are millions of comrades who are willing to vouch for you with their millions of lives and fortunes. Reading the declaration of the Four Supervisors, it is indeed somewhat excessive, but the motivation is entirely for you. The misunderstandings between us have been deep, and there has been no opportunity to sit down and discuss them frankly and without reservation. Therefore, temporary anger is understandable. Now, you advocate resolving Party affairs through the Party, which is a wise statement. Danger turns into safety, and misfortune leans on fortune. The opportunity for a turnaround lies in this. The national crisis is pressing, and no one can survive alone. We must rely on all loyal comrades of the Party, based on the principle of "dying yesterday and living today," to unite sincerely, work together, divide responsibilities, and jointly take responsibility. Then, the future of the Party and the country, unified construction, and so on, will hopefully be achieved. I hope that you will work hard based on this principle, and that the psychology of the future will be transformed in one question, and that harmony and brightness will be realized on the spot. I cannot help but offer my sincere prayers. If my humble opinion is accepted, then I will not hesitate to work hard to mediate in the future, if I am driven. I am terrified at the telegram, and I await your instructions. Your brother, Sun Ke, respectfully. Urgent. Telegram to Gu, Chen, etc.: Extremely urgent, Guangzhou Committee Member Gu Quanqin, Chief Commander Chen Bonan, with respect. Since the Hu case occurred, I have been occupying a position in the Central Government but have been unable to remedy the situation. My mood of depression has turned negative. Therefore, I have been staying at home in Shanghai for more than ten days, declining all engagements. You are far away in Lingnan, and you feel deeply indignant. Therefore, you have proposed impeachment. I am concerned about the current situation and deeply worried that once a dispute arises, the war will be reborn, and unification and peace will once again become a bubble. I have been pacing back and forth, unable to sleep at night. On the day of this month, Brother Tiecheng came to Shanghai with the order of Chairman Chiang, saying that Chairman Chiang had decided to resolve the Guangdong issue within the Party and would not involve military or political matters. Furthermore, Ke's relationship with the Party and the country is extremely close, and at this critical juncture, he should come forward to mediate and should not passively blame. On the day of Wei, I sent a telegram in response. Today, Chairman Chiang entrusted Zhihui, Shizeng, Jingjiang, Yongzhi, and other gentlemen to bring a reply in person, saying that as long as it is beneficial to the revolution and the consolidation of the Party and the country, all good suggestions from comrades can be accepted. He also asked me to convey a telegram from Zhihui and others, signed by five people, to Brother Xiang, and to show me the draft telegrams personally written by Zhan Gong to both of you. Zhan Gong is loyal to the Party and has no peer in history. He advises you not to cause disputes for the sake of one person and to avoid causing suffering to the people. His words are earnest and sincere, and I was moved to tears when I read them. Thinking back to the Northern Expedition of the National Revolutionary Army, countless comrades fought bravely and sacrificed their lives to achieve what we have today. Unless it is absolutely necessary, we should never resort to war again, lest we fail our martyrs, bring disaster to the people, and allow the hidden dangers to grow and become powerful. The Soviet Union has declared to the outside world that China will completely become a Soviet nation within three years. Although this is propaganda, it makes me shudder to think about it. If civil war is truly unavoidable, it will only create opportunities for the Red bandits. The Party will perish and the country will perish. We are all followers of the Three Principles of the People. If there is a glimmer of hope to avoid war, then we should not hesitate to make any personal sacrifices. After thinking about it again and again, I believe that at this critical moment, if it is beneficial to the Party and the country, I would not hesitate to go through fire and water. I can no longer shirk my responsibility to mediate. I plan to go to Nanjing with Zhi, Shi, Jing, and Yong to speak directly to Chairman Chiang, and then discuss with all comrades the way to live in peace with each other. I urge you to maintain silence in Guangdong, stabilize the people's hearts, and not allow the situation to rush towards a difficult resolution. This is my hope. Please let me know your opinions as much as possible, and I will be responsible for mediating. Ze Ru and all comrades send their regards. Your brother, Sun Ke, respectfully.

Chen Mingshu Goes to Japan 138

Stays for a Month or More Before Going to Europe and America

Sun Hiwen Goes to Nanjing Again Last Night

Chen Mingshu, Chairman of the Guangdong Provincial Government, along with his secretary Yang Jianping, left Shanghai for Japan on the British mail ship Kashmir at 7:00 a.m. yesterday. He also specially dispatched his secretary-general, Sun Hiwen, to Nanjing by the 11:45 p.m. night train to meet with Chairman Chiang, report everything on his behalf, and bid farewell. According to Sun, when interviewed by our reporter yesterday:

Unexpected Travel: Chairman Chen has been thinking of traveling abroad, but he has not had the time. When he went to Nanjing last year, he strongly requested Chairman Chiang to allow him to go abroad, but his request was not granted. This spring, he telegraphed again, but it did not materialize. This time, he considered it the only opportunity and resolutely went abroad.

Inspection of Europe and America: Chen has applied for passports for Central Europe and the Americas. He plans to stay in Japan for a month or more, and then decide on his itinerary to Europe and America. However, in any case, he has decided not to return to China for the time being. Even if the Guangdong issue is resolved peacefully, Chen will not repeat the same mistake.

Trip to Jiangxi Not Confirmed: The reporter then asked if it was true that you would be ordered to go to Jiangxi to慰劳 Chiang and Cai's armies. He replied, "I will return to Shanghai within a few days. The trip to Jiangxi is baseless." When asked about Huang Shaoxiong's whereabouts, he replied, "I heard that Ji Lu will also travel to Japan. I don't know anything else."
